## **Common Flower Names**

## **Flower Parts**

Flower names are built on the base name **vos** , meaning _flower_ . First, here is a list of flower parts:

**Flower Parts Flower Parts vos** .... _flower_ **vosayob** .... _sepal_ **vosayeb** .... _petal_ **vosib** .... _receptacle_ **veeybpexus** .... _stigma_ **vosij** .... _bud, flower bud_ **tooygon** .... _pistil_ **veeybyan** .... _pollen_ **twoogon** .... _stamen_ **twoogonyif** .... _filament_ **veeybyem** .... _anther_ **vosyob** .... _peduncle_

## **Less Common Botanical Names**

No Mirad dictionary can reasonably list all flora by name. The less common glosses not given above are derived from the ICN world standard Latin taxonomic names, which can be found at Wikipedia:International_Code_of_Nomenclature_for_algae,_fungi,_and_plants. For example, the _Magnolia grandiflora_ or the _Tulipa suaveolens_ , pictured in the above section. The name are pronounced as they are in Latin, not in Mirad. For example, an _x_ is pronounced _ks_ or _gs_ as in Latin, not _sh_ as in Mirad.

## **Medical and Pharmaceutical Terminology**

This is a vast field where the limited morpheme aggregate of Mirad cannot serve to translate all the technical vocabulary. It will, therefore, translate only very common words and leave the rest in Greco-Latin as do many natural languages.

## **Medical Diseases**

Some common medical conditions can be readily be translated in Mirad using its existing set of morphemes, eg.

**balyoganbok** .... _asthma_ (lit: shortness of breath illness) **tiebbok** .... _pneumonia_ (lit: lung illness) **teibbok** .... _rhinitis_ (lit: nose illness) **tayibblok** .... _neuropathy_ (lit: nerve suffering) **tebbyoyk** .... _headache_ (lit: head ache) **teibzyegikanbok** .... _osteoporosis_ (lit: bone porosity illness)

## **Pharmaceuticals**

Medicines can be referred to by their trade names, some of which have been genericized.

**aspirin** .... _aspirin_ **Ibupropen** .... _Ibupropen_

Others can be translated by words indicating the purpose:

**bukpoyxol, bukkyuxlol** .... _analgesic, painkiller_ (Lit: pain reliever) **tikebilokxol** .... _emetic_ (Lit: vomit-inducing-substance)

Less common drugs, and any drugs for that matter, can be referred to by the official International Nonproprietary Name (INN) (see Nonproprietary Names (https://www.who.int/teams/health-product -and-policy-standards/inn%7CInternational)). For example, _phenobarbital_ . In case a Greco-Roman name is used, the following pronunciation guide applies to Mirad:

121 of 158

Mirad Grammar/print version - Wikibooks, open books for an open world

**==> picture [88 x 150] intentionally omitted <==**

**----- Start of picture text -----**<br>
INN names pronunciation<br>GRECO-ROMAN MIRAD<br>SPELLING PRONUNCIATION<br>ch k<br>ph f<br>x ks<br>y i<br>qu kw<br>rh r<br>th t<br>ae e<br>oe e<br>c before i, e, or y s<br>c otherwise k<br>final e silent<br>double consonant single consonant<br>**----- End of picture text -----**<br>

Examples:

**acetaminophen** .... _a-se-ta-mi-no-FEN_ **amphetamine** .... _am-fe-ta-MIN_ **trimethroprim** .... _tri-me-tro-PRIM_ **sulfamethoxazole** .... _sul-fa-me-to-ksa-ZOL_ **oxacillin** .... _o-ksa-si-LIN_

## **Other Minerals**

All other minerals end in -muk with a prefix related to the 3-letter IMA symbol name (seesubstituted with lower-case Mirad alphabetic spellings. A list of IMA symbols can be found at Warr, L.N. (2021).Wikipedia:List_of_minerals_recognized_by_the_International_Mineralogical_Association"IMA–CNMNC approved mineral symbols". _Mineralogical Magazine_ ). The IMA name is. **85** (3): 291–320. Bibcode:2021MinM...85..291W. doi:10.1180/mgm.2021.43. S2CID 235729616.. For example:

**==> picture [145 x 45] intentionally omitted <==**

**----- Start of picture text -----**<br>
Some Mineral Names<br>ENGLISH IMA SYMBOL MIRAD SPELLINGS MIRAD NAME<br>argyrodyte Agy a-ge-yu ageyumuk<br>brochantyte Bct ba-ca-to bacatomuk<br>chromite Chr ca-he-ro caheromuk<br>**----- End of picture text -----**<br>

There are some minerals having an IMA with a hyphenated suffix of one or two letters. In that case, the extra letters are added to the name (without the hyphen), eg.:

_Lemmleinite-K_ (Lem-k) is **liemikomuk** in Mirad.

## **Rock Classification**

The naming of individual rock types is based on the BGS Rock Classification Scheme. All rocks end in one of the following suffixes, depending on the main type:

**ameg** .... _sedimentary rock_ **emeg** .... _igneous rock_ **imag** .... _metamorphic rock_

The names for obscure rocks are taken from the [Rock Classification Scheme (https://www.bgs.ac.uk/download/bgs-rock-classification-scheme-igneous/%7CBGS)]. The final _e_ is dropped from names that end in _yte_ or _ite_ . For example, _trachydacite_ in the scheme becomes **trachydacit** in Mirad. This word is then followed by one of the rock types above. So _trachydacite_ becomes **trachydacitemeg** in Mirad. For obvious reason, all the thousands of rock names cannot be listed here or included in the Mirad dictionary.

The word **meg** _rock_ has some common sub-elements:

**meag** .... _marble_ **meeg** .... _slate_ **meig** .... _granite_ **meug** .... _clay, dough_

122 of 158

Mirad Grammar/print version - Wikibooks, open books for an open world

**meyog** .... _china_ **meyag** .... _chalk_ **meyeg** .... _limestone_ **meyig** .... _alabaster_ **meyug** .... _gypsum_ **mealog** .... _sandstone, stoneware_ There is also: **megag** .... _boulder_ **megog** .... _stone_ **yanmeg** .... _cement_ **megyog** .... _gravel_ **mameg** .... _coal_ **maameg** .... _anthracite_ **eymameg** .... _coke_ **maemeg** .... _peat_ **maimeg** .... _lignite_ **mieg** .... _pebble_ Related are: **mek** .... _dust_ **miek** .... _sand_ **myek** .... _powder_ **muk** .... _mineral_ **meil** .... _mud_ **mez** .... _gem, crystal_ **muz** .... _ore_

## **Measurements**

Mirad uses the International System of Units|International System of Units (SI) for rendering measurement units. These symbols are pronounced as if you were spelling each letter out (see Mirad Grammar/Phonology and Orthography#Alphabet|the alphabet. Bear in mind that majuscules (uppercase letters are prefaced with the word **ag-** ( _big_ ). Similarly, Greek letters are spelled with the Greek names ( **alpha** , **gamma** , etc.) preceded with the word **ag-** if majuscule ( **aggamma** for _γ_ ) The Mirad equivalent of the SI symbol for _ohm_ (Ω) is **agomega** . All metric units end in the word **nak** .

## **Metrical Formulae**

The following chart shows how in Mirad to pronounce coherent derived unit formulae in terms of base units. Note that the backslash means _per_ or _divided by_ and is pronounced **gol** . The symbol x means _times_ and is pronounced **gal** . The superscript number is a power and is pronounced **gar** plus the number (with **-wa** , if a unit number). The negative superscript number is pronounced **gor** plus the number (again, with **-wa** if a unit number). See Arithmetical Expressions for further information on these terms.

## **Metric Micro and Macro Prefixes**

The SI has a whole list of prefixes that act as multipliers (macro) or dividers (micro) of the above and other measurement units. For example, a _kilometer_ is a meter times a 1,000 (macro unit), whereas a millimeter is a meter divided by a 1,000 (micro unit). The SI symbol for _b_ (byte) is pronounced **ba** in Mirad. A terabyte ( _Tb_ ) is therefore pronounced **ag-to-ba** , which This amounts _10[12] bytes_ . Here is a table showing the Mirad macro and micro prefixes:

**==> picture [289 x 332] intentionally omitted <==**

**----- Start of picture text -----**<br>
Scalar Metrics<br>MACRO MICRO<br>BASE10 US/UK NAME MIRAD PREFIXMIRAD PRON.SI PREFIX SI SYMBOL [BASE] 10 (US/UK NAME) MIRAD PREFIXSI PREFIX MIRAD PRON.SI SYMBOL<br>1 one an-  ...  mono-, uni- 1/1 whole ayn- holo-, uni-<br>2 two en- bi- 1/2 half eyn- demi-, di-<br>3 three in- tri- 1/3 third iyn- terci-<br>4 four un- tetra- 1/4 fourth uyn- quadri-<br>5 five yoon- penta- 1/5 fifth yoyn quinti-<br>6 six yaon- hexa- 1/6 sixth yayn sexti-<br>7 seven yeon- hepta- 1/7 seventh yeyn septi-<br>8 eight yion octo- 1/8 eighth yiyn octi-<br>9 nine yuon nona- 1/9 ninth yuyn novi-<br>10 ten alo- deca- da da-a- 1/10 tenth aloy- deci- d da-<br>10 [2] hundred aso- hexa- h hi- 10 [-2] hundredth asoy- centi- c ca-<br>10 [3] thousand amso- kilo- k ki- 10 [-3] thousandth) amsoy- milli- m mi-<br>10 [6] million amlo- mega- M agmi- 10 [-6] millionth amloy- micro- r ro-<br>10 [9] billion /milliard amro- giga- G agge- 10 [-9] billionth/ milliardth amroy- nano- n ni-<br>10 [12] trillion /billion garale- tera- T agto- 10 [-12] trillionth / billionth) gorale- pico- p po-<br>10 [15] quadrillion)/ billiard garalyo- peta- P agpo- 10 [-15] quadrillionth) / billiardth goralyo- femto- f fe-<br>10 [18] quintillion / trillion garalyu- exa- E age- 10 [-18] quintillionth)/ trillionth goralyu atto- a a-<br>10 [21] sextillion)/ trilliard garela- zetta- Z agzu- 10 [-21] sextillionth / trilliardth gorela zepto- z zu-<br>10 [24] septillion)/ quadrillion garelu- yotta- Y agyu 10 [-27] septillionth / quadrillionth gorelu yocto- y yu-<br>**----- End of picture text -----**<br>

*Note: The **gar** ( _to a plus power_ ) and **gor** ( _to a minus power_ ) forms are alternatives for the numeric prefixes beyond 100. For example, _billion_ (10[9] ) could be expressed as **garyu-** (ten) to the 9th power _, while_ billionth _could be expressed by_ _**goryu** (_ (ten) to the minus 9th power). The prefix **garya-** is composed of the positive exponential operator **gar** ( _to the power of_ ), followed by the number _6_ . The prefix **gorale-** is composed of the negative exponential operator **gor** ( _to the root of_ ), followed by the number _12_ .

## **Forming Adjectives**

You can form an adjective by adding the suffix **a** to a substantive, adverb, or preposition. By substantive is meant a noun, pronoun, or gerund. Any of these can be adjectivized. Examples:

## **Adjectival Prefixes**

## **Negating the Meaning of Adjectives**

The semantics of an adjective can be reversed with the prefix **o-** . Examples: **vlea** .... _probable_ → **ovlea** .... _improbable_ **fika** .... _perfect_ → **ofika** .... _imperfect_ **twa** .... _known_ → **otwa** .... _unknown_ **bosa** .... _quiet_ → **obosa** .... _upset, unquiet_ Note: Occasionally, the prefix **lo-** is used to avoid ambiguity, as in the following case: **fwa** .... _wanted_ → **ofwa** .... _prohibited_ < **ofer** .... _to prohibit_ → **yofwa** .... _impossible_ < **yofer** .... _to be unable_ → **lofwa** .... _unwanted_ < **fer** .... _to want_ (disambiguated) The prefixes **lyo-** and **ov** are more intense for reversing the meaning of an adjective: **data** .... _friendly_ **odata** .... _unfriendly_ **ovdata** .... _hostile_ **lyodata** .... _inimical_ **dota** .... _social_ **odota** .... _unsocial_ **ovdota** .... _antisocial_ **lyodota** .... _savage_

## **Forming Adverbs**

Adjectives can be converted into adverbs by post-y-gliding the adjectival suffix **a** , in other words, by adding a **y** to the adjective. Adverbs modify verbs, adjectives, and other adverbs. Examples:

**==> picture [87 x 65] intentionally omitted <==**

**----- Start of picture text -----**<br>
Deriving Adverbs<br>ADJECTIVE ADVERB<br>fia .... good fiay .... well<br>vyaa .... true vyaay .... truly<br>gyua .... easy gyuay .... easily<br>iga .... quick igay .... quickly<br>auta .... personal autay .... personally<br>**----- End of picture text -----**<br>

For brevity's sake, the stem of monosyllabic de-adjectival adverbs can be used at the end of a clause or sentence. For example:

**It tyoyape ig.** .... _He walks fast._ **Yit xa has fi.** .... _They did it well._

## **Special Adverbs**

Mirad has special adverbs that are not derived from adjectives and may or may not end in **-ay** .

Here are the principal such adverbs:

129 of 158

Mirad Grammar/print version - Wikibooks, open books for an open world

**==> picture [136 x 253] intentionally omitted <==**

**----- Start of picture text -----**<br>
Special Adverbs<br>MIRAD ENGLISH<br>vay indeed, really, certainly, do  (cf.  va .... yes )<br>vey possibly, may, might  (cf.  ve .... maybe )<br>voy not  (cf.  vo .... no )<br>ga more  (modifying an adjective, adverb, or verb)<br>gay also, moreover, further, still<br>ge as, equally  (modifying an adjective, adverb, or verb)<br>gey even<br>go less  (modifying an adjective, adverb, or verb)<br>goy no longer, no more<br>gla very<br>glay quite, rather, so<br>gle so<br>glo not very, not so<br>gra too<br>gre enough, sufficiently, over-<br>gro not...enough, inadequately, under-<br>gwa most, super-<br>gwe average<br>gwo least, sub-<br>zay ahead, forward<br>zey across<br>zoy back<br>zye through<br>zya throughout<br>**----- End of picture text -----**<br>

The first three adverbs in the above chart are used to affirm or emphasize, cast doubt on, or negate verb predicates as in the examples that follow:

AFFIRMATIVE: **Va, at vay se taduwa.** .... _Yes, I am indeed married._ DUBITIVE: **Iyta dud se vey vyosa.** .... _Her response is possibly wrong._ NEGATIVE: **At voy se eta yuxrut.** .... _I am not your slave._

The adverbs above beginning with **g** are quantitative adverbs and modify an adjective, verb, or another adverb:

**Et se gla via.** .... _You are very beautiful [=ADJECTIVE]._ **Et peya gra ig.** .... _You were going too fast [=ADVERB]._ **It gra dale.** .... _He talks [=VERB] too much._

Other special adverbs, which do not end in **-ay** , include the following, which can all be used in multi-word prepositions:

Look down to the ground.<br>yub .... near Besu yub bi ha mas. .... Stay near the wall.<br>yib .... far Ha tobi igpia yib bi ha yovbyokam. .... ## **Pro-adverbs**

There are also adverbial expressions that are formed with deictic prefixes and categorical stubs to produce what are known as _**pro-adverbs**_ . These include interrogative pro-adverbs like **duhom?** ( _where?_ ), **duhoyen?** ( _how?_ ), **duhoj?** ( _when?_ ), **duhogla** ( _to what extent?_ ), and their answers, such as **hum** ( _there_ ), **heyen** ( _somehow_ ), and **hyoj** ( _never_ ), **hugla** ( _so, to that extent_ ). These words are discussed under the chapter on Deictic Determiners.

Verbs can be formed from various parts of speech: Noun stems Adjective stems Verb stems

## **Forming Verbs from Nouns**

Verbs can often be formed from nouns simply by adding the verb infinitive suffix **er** :

Denominal Verb Derivation<br>NOUN VERB<br>syag .... count syager .... to count<br>af .... permission afer .... may, be allowed<br>teud .... cry, shout teuder .... to cry, shout, exclaim<br>taj .... birth tajer .... to be born<br>tej .... life tejer .... to live<br>toj .... death tojer .... to die<br>ej .... present ejer .... to continue<br>ij .... beginning ijer .... to begin<br>uj .... end ijer .... to end<br>yuj .... sleep tujer .... to sleep<br>**----- End of picture text -----**<br>

## **Verb Formants**

More often, an auxiliary verb or verb stub is used to create various verbs from nouns. The most common such _**verb formants**_ are in this chart:

- **-ser** .... _to be/become_ usually intransitive and stative ( _unite_ = _become one_ )

- **-xer** .... _to do/make_ usually transitive and dynamic ( _unite_ = _make one_ )

- **-per** .... _to go_ usually intransitive and a dynamic verb of motion ( _mount_ = _get onto_ )

- **-ber** .... _to put_ usually transitive and a verb of gesture ( _apply_ = _put onto_ )

- **-ier** a stub from the verb _to take_ , usually an action verb benefiting the agent ( _eat_ = _take food_ )

- **-uer** a stub from the verb _to give_ , usually an action verb benefiting the patient ( _feed_ = _give food_ )

- **-der** .... _to say_ , a verb of communication ( _affirm_ = _say yes_ )

- **-ter** .... _to know_ , verbs of the perception and knowledge ( **teater** = _see_ )

Some of the above formants can be intensified with the liquids **l** or **r** , eg. **sler, -xler, -xrer, -bler, -prer** .

**==> picture [241 x 451] intentionally omitted <==**

**----- Start of picture text -----**<br>
Verb Derivation with Verb Formants<br>NOUN AUXILIARY VERB OR VERB STUB FORMANT VERB<br>yav .... innocence der .... to say yavder .... to acquit<br>yov .... shame, guilt aber .... to apply, put on yovaber .... to shame, accuse<br>yov .... shame, guilt ober .... to remove, take off yovober .... to excuse, exculpate<br>tof .... clothes aber .... to apply, put on tofaber .... to dress, don<br>tof .... clothes ober .... to remove, take off tofober .... to undress, strip<br>det .... associate ser .... to be, become detser .... to associate<br>dat .... friend xer .... to do, make datxer .... to befriend<br>san .... form ser .... to be, become sanser .... to form (intransitive)<br>san .... form xer .... to do, make sanxer .... to form (transitive)<br>tel .... food (b)ier .... to take telier .... to eat, consume<br>tel .... food (b)uer .... to give teluer .... to feed, nourish<br>if .... pleasure (b)ier .... to take ifier .... to enjoy<br>if .... pleasure (b)uer .... to give ifuer .... to please<br>taj .... birth ber .... to put tajber .... to give birth<br>tej .... life per .... to go tejper .... to come alive<br>tej .... life ber .... to put tejber .... to bring to life<br>toj .... death per .... to go tojper .... to drop dead<br>toj .... death ber .... to put tojber .... to kill<br>tij .... wakefulness per .... to go tijper .... to wake up<br>tij .... wakefulness ber .... to put tijber .... to awaken<br>tuj .... sleep per .... to go tujper .... to fall asleep<br>tuj .... sleep ber .... to put tujber .... to put to sleep<br>tax .... memory (b)ier .... to take taxier .... to recall<br>tax .... memory (b)uer .... to give taxuer .... to remind<br>yev .... justice der .... to say, tell yevder .... to judge<br>vyan .... truth der .... to say, tell vyander .... to tell the truth<br>vyon .... falsehood der .... to say, tell vyonder .... to tell a lie<br>il .... liquid aker .... to gain ilaker .... to take on liquid<br>il .... liquid oker .... to lose iloker .... to leak, lose liquid<br>il .... liquid (b)ier .... to take ilier .... to soak up<br>il .... liquid (b)uer .... to give iluer .... to pour, water<br>il .... liquid ikser .... to get full ilikser .... to be soaked  (intransitive)<br>il .... liquid ikxer .... to fill up ilikxer .... to flood, soak  (transitive)<br>il .... liquid ukser .... to become empty ilukser .... to drain  (intransitive)<br>il .... liquid ukxer .... to empty ilukxer .... to flush  (transitive)<br>il .... liquid ser .... to be, become ilser .... to liquify, melt  (intransitive)<br>il .... liquid xer .... to do, make ilxer .... to liquify, melt  (transitive)<br>il .... liquid aber .... to apply, put on ilaber .... to wash  (transitive)<br>il .... liquid aper .... to get on ilaper .... to float  (intransitive)<br>il .... liquid per .... to go ilper .... to flow  (intransitive)<br>il .... liquid zyaber .... to spread ilzyaber .... to spray, shower  (transitive)<br>il .... liquid zyober .... to squeeze ilzyober .... to squirt  (transitive)<br>il .... liquid pyexer .... to strike ilpyexer .... to splash (with liquid)<br>il .... liquid yujer .... to close ilyujer .... to plug<br>**----- End of picture text -----**<br>

Note that verbs ending in **-ser** and **-ier** are intransitive (they take no object), while those ending in **-xer** and **-uer** are transitive. Also, **-ier** verbs are inchoative, while **-uer** verbs are benefactive or causative (making someone do something).

## **Forming Verbs from Adjectives With -xer and -ser**

The verbs that are formed from adjectives fall mainly into two groups, the transitive group with **-xer** .... _to do, make, cause_ , and the intransitive group with **-ser** .... _to be, become_ .

131 of 158

Mirad Grammar/print version - Wikibooks, open books for an open world

The following chart shows how these verbs are formed:

**==> picture [189 x 64] intentionally omitted <==**

**----- Start of picture text -----**<br>
Forming Verbs with Xer and Ser<br>ADJECTIVE TRANSITIVE VERB INTRANSITIVE VERB<br>aza .... strong azaxer .... fortify, strengthen, make strong azaser .... get strong<br>oza .... week ozaxer .... weaken ozaser .... grow weaker<br>kyia .... heavy kyiaxer .... weigh down kyiaser .... grow heavy<br>kyua .... light kyuaxer .... lighten, make lighter kyuaser .... get lighter<br>yana .... together yanaxer .... bring together yanaser .... get together<br>**----- End of picture text -----**<br>

The final adjective ending **a** is often dropped to form a verb with a slightly different meaning, usually somewhat more idiomatic. In some cases, dropping the **a** makes it clear that the verb is created from a noun rather than an adjective, as in the last example of the following chart:

## **Forming Verbs of Gesture and Motion with -ber and -per**

Verbs of gesture are formed with the transitive auxiliary verb **ber** .... _to put_ , while parallel verbs of motion are formed with the intransitive auxiliary verb **per** .... _to go_ . These verbs are usually paired and are often built from a prepositional base. If the prepositional base ends in **b** , the **b** is dropped. Here are some examples:

**==> picture [183 x 241] intentionally omitted <==**

**----- Start of picture text -----**<br>
Verb Derivation with Ber and Per<br>PREPOSITONBASE TRANSITIVE GESTURE VERB INTRANSITIVE MOTION VERB<br>ab .... on aber .... apply, put on aper .... mount, get on<br>eb .... between eber .... block eper .... intervene<br>ob .... off ober .... remove, take off oper .... dismount, get off<br>ib .... away iber .... receive iper .... leave<br>ub .... toward uber .... send uper .... come<br>yab .... up yaber .... raise yaper .... rise<br>yeb .... in yeber .... insert yeper .... enter<br>oyeb .... out oyeber .... take out oyeper .... exit<br>yob .... down yober .... lower yoper .... descend<br>yib .... far yiber .... take away yiper .... move away<br>yub .... near yuber .... bring yuper .... approach<br>za .... front zaber .... put up front zaper .... take the lead<br>zay .... forward zayber .... advance zayper .... advance, go forward<br>ze .... middle zeber .... balance zeper .... balance<br>zey .... across zeyber .... take across, transfer zeyper .... cross, go over, transit<br>zo .... behind zober .... hinder zoper .... trail, lag<br>zoy .... back zoyber .... set back, return zoyper .... retreat, go back, return<br>iz .... straight izber .... guide izper .... aim for<br>uz .... crooked uzber .... divert uzper .... turn, diverge<br>zu .... left zuber .... set to the left zuper ....  go left<br>yiz .... beyond yizber .... take beyond yizper .... pass by<br>yuz .... around yuzber .... take around yuzper .... go around<br>**----- End of picture text -----**<br>

More elaborate verbs of gesture and motion can be formed by adding positional/directional ordinal vowels along with combinations of **ser** and **xer** , plus the intensifiers **y** , **l** and **r** . In this more complex scheme, the stem-initial **p** is a more semantically intense version of **b** . Also the verb endings **-sler** and **-srer** and more intense versions of the intransitive ending **-ser** , while **-xler** and **-xrer** and more intense version of the transitve ending **-xer** . Verbs ending in **-ler** and **-rer** are transitive voice by nature, **-rer** being more semantically intense. Prepositions can be prefixed to change the direction of the gestures or motions.

hold<br>bexler .... keep<br>baler .... press<br>yanbaler .... compress<br>baer .... lean on yobaleryuzbaler ........ depress, suppresshug paer .... hover<br>zoybaler .... repress<br>barer .... ## Mirad Grammar/Word Families

## **Word Order**

Overall, Mirad is an _**SVO**_ language, that is, the normal word order is _**Subject + Verb Predicate + Object**_ , much like English and all of the Romance languages. The subject and object consist of nouns or pronouns with or without modifiers. The verb predicate consists of a conjugated verb form with or without adverbial modifiers, which may precede or follow based on considerations below.

## **The Subject**

A subject is the entity that is responsible for the action or state in the verb predicate. That entity consists of modified or unmodified zero or more nouns or pronouns. The subject can be a noun phrase, which can include modifiers like deictic adjectives, quantifiers, or descriptive adjectives preceding a noun or nouns heading up a prepositional phrase.

135 of 158

Mirad Grammar/print version - Wikibooks, open books for an open world

**==> picture [286 x 246] intentionally omitted <==**

**----- Start of picture text -----**<br>
Some rules:<br>Modifiers of a noun or noun phrase precede that noun or noun phrase:<br>Deictic adjectives and possessive pronouns come in first place among the modifiers:<br>Hia via toyb .... this beautiful woman<br>Ha aa dresiun .... the first letter<br>Yata ifwa twed hu toja zojub .... our beloved father who died last year<br>Quantifiers come after any deictic adjectives or possessive pronouns, but before the noun they modify:<br>Hua ewa pati .... those two birds<br>Hya ha gla jubi .... all the many days<br>Iyta gla yafoni .... her many abilities<br>Prepositions precede their complement:<br>Za ata tam .... in front of my house<br>Prepositional phrase modifiers follow the noun they modify:<br>ha domep zo yata tam .... the street behind our house<br>saxam yub bi et .... a factory near you<br>Relative clause modifiers follow the noun or noun phrase they modify:<br>Hos at voy teste .... the thing (that) I don't understand<br>Ha glo doymi ho zoybese .... the few towns that remain<br>A subject noun can consist of a clause, infinitive, or gerund:<br>Van it upo se vala. .... That he will come is certain.<br>Ser yiva se ser iva. .... To be free is to be happy.<br>Hia uvteuden yefe poser. .... This weeping must stop.<br>The subject can consist of a pronoun or linked pronouns:<br>Et ay at .... You and I<br>Anay et .... Only you<br>Glati .... many people<br>Adverbs often precede what they modify, but this rule is somewhat loose.<br>gey et .... even you<br>deuzen fiay .... singing well<br>voy aken .... not winning<br>**----- End of picture text -----**<br>

**==> picture [57 x 64] intentionally omitted <==**

## **Prepositional Phrases**

In Mirad, prepositional phrases consist of a simple or complex (= multi-word) preposition followed by a complement. Some examples: **be moj** .... _at night_ (simple)

**ja utyal** .... _before supper_ (simple) **yeb bu ha tam** .... _into the house_ (complex)

## **Use of Simple Prepositions**

Mirad has the following simple prepositions, which, except for **ogel** , are monosyllabic, and stand directly before their substantive complement:

**==> picture [283 x 389] intentionally omitted <==**

**----- Start of picture text -----**<br>
Simple Prepositions<br>ab .... on eb .... between ob .... off ib .... away from ub .... toward<br>ayb .... above eyb .... among oyb .... under<br>be .... at bi .... of, from bu .... to<br>bay .... with bey .... by, via boy .... without byi .... from the start of byu ... up to<br>za .... in front of ze .... in the middle of zo .... behind zi .... at the right of zu .... at the left of<br>zya .... throughout zye .... through<br>ja .... before je .... during jo .... after ji .... since ju .... until<br>gab .... plus gob .... minus<br>gal .... times gel .... like gol .... divided by<br>ogel .... unlike<br>gar .... to the power of gor .... to the root (negative power) of<br>ay .... and ey .... or oy .... but<br>av .... for ov .... against<br>ayv .... about oyv .... opposite<br>vyel .... about, than, as<br>Examples:<br>boy uvteuden .... without moaning<br>av hyea tesdud .... for whatever reason<br>ewa gal ewa .... two times two<br>poper zya Europam. .... to travel all over Europe.<br>iwa gar se yuwa .... three squared is nine<br>yekea dyes vyel(or: ayv) Mirad .... looking for a book about Mirad<br>The preposition  be  ( at ) is used as an all-purpose locator:<br>be ha mimkum .... at the beach<br>be ha domep .... in the street<br>be ha meb .... on the mountain<br>be Fransam .... in France<br>The preposition  be  is used in many idioms, where  ha  ( the ) is omitted:<br>be dropek bay .... at war with<br>be obem bi .... at the bottom of ( = at bottom of)<br>be nem bi .... in place of, instead of, in lieur of<br>be tam bi .... chez, at the house of<br>be zam bi .... in front of<br>be sinibar .... on television<br>be dud bu .... in response to<br>be tam .... at home<br>The preposition  bi  can be used for  from , indicating origin, or  of , denoting possession or origin.<br>Examples:<br>Ata twed zoypa bi yex gwa. .... My father returned from work early.<br>Ha yabtom bi London se humep. .... The tower of London is that way.<br>His se ha dyes bi hua twob. .... This is that man's book ( = the book of that man).<br>**----- End of picture text -----**<br>

The proposition **to** ( _to_ ) can often be omitted after a verb where the **to-ness** is embedded in the verb. This omission is possible only when the verb is followed immediately by the object of destination:

Examples:

136 of 158

Mirad Grammar/print version - Wikibooks, open books for an open world

**Buu at hua drar.** ... _Give me that pencil (or: Buu hua drar bu at.)_

**Pu tam!** .... _Go home! (but: Pu izay bu tam!)_

**At peye zedom.** .... _I am going downtown. (or: At peye bu zedom.)_ The preposition **vyel** is used for two purposes:

_about, concerning, relative to_ as in **Hia dyes vyel moltun se yika.** .... _This book about physics is difficult._

_than, as_ after comparative adjectives as in **ga aga vyel huas** .... _bigger than that one_ .

Do not confuse **bay** and **bey** , both of which can sometimes be translated by _with_ in English.

**bay** denotes accompaniment as in **Duven et po bay at?** .... _Will you be going with me?_

**bey** denotes means as in **It pyexa at bey muf.** .... _He hit me with ( = by means of) a stick._

The above simple prepositions can be used with adverbs to form more complex prepositions. The following chart shows adverbs which ban be joined with simple prepositions to create complex prepositions:

## **Using Prepositions as Clausal Conjunctions**

Some simple and complex prepositions can introduce a dependent clause, but must be followed by the positive particle **van** . This rule does not apply to **ay** ( _and_ ), **ey** ( _or_ ) and **oy** ( _but_ ), because they are already properly conjunctions. This chart shows some examples:

**==> picture [253 x 104] intentionally omitted <==**

**----- Start of picture text -----**<br>
Prepositions as Clausal Conjunctions<br>PREPOSITION CLAUSAL CONJUNCTION EXAMPLE<br>ja before ja van It tojo  He will die ja van before  et puo.  you arrive.<br>je je van Je van et tuxeya, at tujeya.<br>during while While you were studying, I was sleeping.<br>jo after jo van Yit xo ifonpop  They will go on a honeymoon ja van yit tadso. after they get married.<br>av van Egxu av van et su jwabwa.<br>av so that Rehearse so that you will be prepared.<br>for av von Yexu jestay av von et ujoku.<br>lest...not, so that...not Study hard so you won't fail.<br>ov (gey) ov van It igpa gey ov van it ta van it so gwaa.<br>against (even) though, despite the fact that He (or she) ran even though he knew (that) he would be late.<br>**----- End of picture text -----**<br>

Note that **av van** and **av von** are followed by a clause where the predicate verb is in the hypothetical mood ( **-u** ), reminiscent of the subjunctive in the Romance languages.

## **The Predicate**

The predicate consists of a verb, its modifiers, and its objects.

## **Rules**

The adverbs **vay** ( _indeed_ ), **vey** ( _possibly, may_ ), and **voy** ( _not_ ) usually precede the verb: **Yata tam voy osexwa.** .... _Our house was not destroyed._ **Vey mamilo.** .... _It may rain._ **Et se vay fia deuzut.** .... _You are really a fine singer._

Other adverbs and come either before or after the verb, depending on emphasis.

**Dalu yug!** .... _Speak softly!_ **Et dale gra ig.** .... _You speak too fast._ **It glaxag ake.** .... _He often wins._ **Glaxag it ake.** .... _Often he wins._ **It ake glaxag.** .... _He wins often._

Yes-no questions are formed by preceding the verb predicate with **Duven...?** , which means _Say whether..., Is it true that..._ , without any word order change in the verb predicate: **Duven it gaj tejeye?** .... _Is (it true that) he still living?_ **Duven et te ha dud?** .... _Do you know the answer?_

Questions words requiring fill-in-the-blank words like _When?_ , _Where?_ , _Who?_ , etc. start out with the question word, followed by the verb predicate in unchanged word order: **Duhoj et taja?** .... _When were you born?_ **Duhoyen et se?** .... _How are you?_ **Duhos se eta dyun?** .... _What is your name?_ **Duhom et tambee?** .... _Where do you live?_ **Duhot kobia ata dyes?** .... _Who stole my book?_

137 of 158

Mirad Grammar/print version - Wikibooks, open books for an open world

Question words that are adverbs, as well as pronominal question words that are the subject of a stative predicate, can appear at the end of a sentence: **Et taja duhoj?** .... _When were you born?_ **Et se duhoyen?** .... _How are you?_ **Eta dyun se duhos?** .... _What is your name?_ **Et tambee duhom?** .... _Where do you live?_ Verbs can be serial: **It deuze, daze, ay duzare.** .... _He sings, dances, and plays an instrument._ **Eku ey pilu!** .... _Play or get lost!_ **Iyt eka oy oka.** .... _She played but lost._ Verb predicates can have an implied, unexpressed subject: **Mamilo.** .... _(It) is going to rain._ **Upu!** .... _(You) come!_ **Se ama him.** .... _(It) is hot here._ **Voy se yeva jayevder hes.** .... _(It) is not fair to prejudge someone._ **Von (et) jwosu.** .... _Don't (you) be late._ **ypeses** Predicate types, i.e. _**illocutions**_ , refer to how the verb, predicate, clause, or sentence is expressed, There are three predicate types in Mirad: Declarative Interrogative Imperative / Hortative These predicate types, in turn, can be: Negative, or Affirmative, or Combinations of these. A simple, non-negative statement is affirmative declarative, such as **Ha meir yuzpe ha maar.** .... _The earth goes around the sun._

## **Predicate Typeses**

The following sections discuss non-declarative and non-affirmative predicate types.

## **Making Predicates Interrogative**

To make a declarative predicate or sentence into a question, simply begin it with the Yes/No Question Introducer **Duven** .... _Say whether.../Is it true that...?_ or any other interrogative pronoun or adverb such as **Duhos?** .... _What?_ , **Duhot?** .... _Who(m)?_ , or **Duhom?** .... _where?_ . Note that the **Du** in **Duven** means _Say.../ Tell me..._ , so **Duven...?** really is a command meaning _Say whether..._ . The word **ven** without the **du** is a conditional complementizer and just means _if_ or _whether_ . The part of the sentence after **Duven** is a simple declarative statement in the normal word order. The same is true for the words following other interrogative words, such as **Duhos?** .... _What?_ and **Duhom?** .... _Where?_ . In other words, there is no inversion of word order in questions as there often is in English, Spanish, and many other languages.

**==> picture [179 x 92] intentionally omitted <==**

**----- Start of picture text -----**<br>
Making Predicates Interrogative<br>DECLARATIVE INTERROGATIVE<br>Et se tadxwa. Duven et se tadxwa?<br>You are married. Are you married? (= Say whether you are married.)<br>Ha mari se manika. Duven ha mari se manika?<br>The stars are bright. Are the stars bright? (= Say whether the stars are bright.)<br>Hut aka. Duhot aka?<br>That guy won. Who won?<br>Iyt aka glas. Duhoglas iyt aka?<br>She won a lot. How much did she win?<br>It paye. Duhom it paye?<br>He has gone. Where has he gone?<br>**----- End of picture text -----**<br>

**==> picture [31 x 50] intentionally omitted <==**

Note that the question words introduce the sentence and do not alter the word order as seen in the declarative. Also, a declarative sentence can be made interrogative simply by adding a question mark at the end in writing or raising the voice inflection at the end in speaking, eg:

## **Et tambese ha yubem?**

_You live in the neighborhood?_

The yes-no tag **vao** can be placed at the end of a declaration to make it a question, eg.:

**Et tambese ha yubem, vao?** _You live in the neighborhood, right?_ Yes/no questions such as the above and those introduced with **Duven** usually are answered with **va** _yes_ , **ve** _maybe_ , or **vo** _no_ or their equivalents.

**==> picture [162 x 93] intentionally omitted <==**

**----- Start of picture text -----**<br>
"Yes-or-no Questions"<br>YES-NO QUESTION ANSWER<br>Duven eta dyun se John? Vo, se Bill.<br>Is your name John? No, it's Bill.<br>Duven eta apet aka? Va. Atas vay aka.<br>Did your horse win? Yes. Mine won indeed.<br>Duven et texe van ha maalyen gafiso hijub? Ve.<br>Do you think the weather will improve today? Maybe.<br>Fe per bay at? Vey zajub.<br>Wanna go with me? Maybe tomorrow.<br>Et tadso, vao? Vey va, vey vo.<br>You're going to get married, right? Maybe yes, maybe no.<br>**----- End of picture text -----**<br>

## **Affirming/ Doubting / Negating Declarations**

The following set of interjections and adverbs can be used to affirm, cast doubt on, or negate declarations:

**==> picture [188 x 62] intentionally omitted <==**

**----- Start of picture text -----**<br>
Affirming, Doubting, Negative Declarations<br>INTERJECTION ADVERB PROPOSITION<br>AFFIRMATIVE va yes vay indeed, really Va. At Yes, I indeed/do/really  vay yantexe agree.<br>DUBITATIVE ve vey Ve. At vey po.<br>maybe, perhaps possibly, may... Maybe. I may/possibly will go.<br>NEGATIVE vo no voy not Vo. At No. I would voy su iva. not be happy.<br>**----- End of picture text -----**<br>

## **Mixing Them Up**

The above interrogative words and the words of affirmation / doubt / negation can be used in various combinations, for example:

138 of 158

Mirad Grammar/print version - Wikibooks, open books for an open world

**Duven et voy se tadxwa?** .... _Aren't you married?_ **Duhasav iyt se voy tadxwa?** .... _Why isn't she married?_ **Vey voy mamilo.** .... _It may not rain._ **At vay voy tadso iyt.** .... _I will certainly not marry her._ **Et peyo, vao?** .... _You will go, right?_ **Vo. Hus vey vay se vyoa.** .... _No. That may indeed be wrong._ **Et te ha dud, vao?** .... _You know the answer, don't you?_ (= _right?_ )

Note that the particles of affirmation/doubt/negation usually precede the verb, but can just as easily follow it.

**At voy te.** .... _I don't know._ **At te voy.** .... _I don't know. [Lit: I know not.]_

Note that **vao?** is a particle meaning _yes or no?, right?, n'est-ce pas?_

## **Imperative and Hortative Expressions**

An _**imperative**_ expression is a command. In Mirad, a verb in the tenseless hypothetical mood ending in **-u** without a subject is assumed to an imperative referring implicitly to _you_ . For example:

**Ipu !** .... _Go away!_ **Tiju !** .... _Wake up!_ **Su fiat !** .... _Be a good person!_

_**Hortative**_ expressions, i.e. urging or wishing expressions like _Let's go._ or _May he win._ , use the hypothetical form of the verb with the clause introduced by the positive complementizer **van** .... _that, may, let_ . In Arabic and some other languages, this is called the _**jussive**_ mood.

**==> picture [81 x 54] intentionally omitted <==**

**Van yat fadilu.** .... _Let's pray._ (Lit: _That we would pray._ )

**Van weti aku hia ifek.** .... _May you guys win this game._

**Van ha edeb yagteju.** .... _Long live the king._ (Lit. _That the king would long-live._ )

**At ojfe van wit piu.** .... _I wish he'd leave._ (Lit. _I wish that he would leave._ )

The negative version of imperative and hortative expressions is introduced with the negative complementizer **von** .... _don't, lest, let's not_ . If there is no subject pronoun, _you_ is understood.

**Von (et) dalu at huyen.** .... _Don't (you) speak to me that way._ **Von yit oku.** .... _May they not lose._ **Yit fiyake von yet oku.** .... _We hope (_ that _) you will_ not _will._ **Von yat toxu it.** .... _Let's not forget him._

## **Complementizers**

**Van** , **ven** , **von** , and **ho** are complementizers.

**==> picture [322 x 135] intentionally omitted <==**

**----- Start of picture text -----**<br>
Complementizers<br>TYPE COMPLEMENTIZERS MEANING EXAMPLEMIRAD EQUIVALENTENGLISH<br>Is it true that...?<br>Interrogative duven...? Tell (me) whether... Duven eta dyun se John? Is (it true that) your name is John?<br>(yes/no question introducer)<br>Conditional ven if, whether VenAt utdide et te, du has.ven it upo. IfI wonder  you know, say so.whether he'll come.<br>Anti-Conditional oven unless Oven et yexe, et voy ako. Unless you work, you will not win.<br>At ta van it upo. I knew (that) he would come.<br>Positive/Hortative van that, so that, let, may VanVan yat dilo. et su iva. LetLet's pray. you be happy.<br>At xa has van et fitexu at. I did it so you'd think well of me.<br>Von teaxu at. Don't look at me.<br>Negative/Prohibitive von Don't, let...not, lest Von yat su uva. Let's not be sad.<br>At pio von et futipsu. I will leave lest you get angry.<br>Ha toybi ho ifaye et... The women who have loved you.<br>Relative ho who, whom, that, which Ha toyb ho et ife. The woman (whom) you love.<br>Koxon ho at yofe lonyafxer. A problem (that/which) I cannot solve.<br>**----- End of picture text -----**<br>

## **Subjunctive Clauses**

The hypothetical mood is also used in subjunctive clauses. A subjunctive clause is one in which an action or state is desired, requested, required, or wanted in some other way by the actor in the main clause. Positive subjunctive clauses are introduced with the positive complementizer **van** .... _that, let's, so that_ . Here are some examples:

**Ha edweb dira van at tyoibu za it.** .... _The king demanded that I kneel before him._ **Se igefwa van et upu gwa ig.** .... _It is urgent that you come as soon as possible._ **Durwa van hyat dolu.** .... _It was ordered that everyone be silent._

A negative subjunctive clause is introduced with the negative complementizer **von** .... _don't, lest_ .

**Biksu von et pyosu.** .... _Be careful lest you fall / that you not fall._

The conditional complementizer **ven** .... _if, whether_ can introduce a clause in the subjunctive, indicating an unreal condition, as in the following examples:

**At sexu tam ven at su nasika.** .... _I would build a house if I were (= would be) rich._ **Duhas et xu ven et beu ga nas?** .... _What would you do if you had (= would have) more money?_

Many of the above sentences could be rephrased with an infinitive in order to avoid the subjunctive:

**Ha edweb dira at tyoiber za it.** .... _The king demanded me to kneel before him._ **Se igefwa av et uper gwa ig.** .... _It is urgent for you to come as soon as possible._ **Hyat durwa doler.** .... _Everyone was ordered to be silent._ **Biksu voy pyoser.** .... _Be careful not to fall._

## **If-Then Conditional Clauses**

A conditional clause is introduced with the conditional complementizer **ven** .... _if, whether_ . The if-clause can be a real tense or a hypothetical. If the if-clause is hypothetical, the then-clause is also hypothetical. Here are the possible variations:

139 of 158

Mirad Grammar/print version - Wikibooks, open books for an open world

**==> picture [146 x 149] intentionally omitted <==**

**----- Start of picture text -----**<br>
If-then Conditional Clauses<br>IF-CLAUSE THEN-CLAUSE<br>PRESENT INDICATIVE PRESENT INDICATIVE<br>Ven ot yexe gla, ot akxe.<br>If one works hard, one succeeds.<br>PAST INDICATIVE PAST INDICATIVE<br>Ven et ta, et dola.<br>If you knew, you kept quiet.<br>FUTURE INDICATIVE FUTURE INDICATIVE<br>Ven et pio, at so uva.<br>If you leave, I will be sad.<br>PRESENT HYPOTHETICAL PRESENT HYPOTHETICAL<br>Ven at su nyaza, at nuxbiu aga tam.<br>If I were rich, I would buy a new house.<br>Ven et teetu, et testu.<br>If you would listen, you would understand.<br>PAST HYPOTHETICAL PAST HYPOTHETICAL<br>Ven at tayu, at dudayu hyuyen.<br>If I had known, I would have responded differently.<br>**----- End of picture text -----**<br>

**==> picture [73 x 94] intentionally omitted <==**

Note that in English, when the then-clause is future tense, the if-clause is present; This is not the case in Mirad, where both clauses are in the future. In Mirad, the formula is "If you WILL leave, I WILL be sad." In English, the formula "I didn't know whether he WOULD x" is translated in Mirad as "I didn't know whether he WILL x."

## **If/Whether Subordinate Clauses**

Here are some examples of sentences where the main clause contains some verb of _knowing, questioning, wondering, guessing_ followed by a subordinate clause introduced by the conditional complementizer **ven** .... _whether / if_ . Note that the tenses in Mirad are somewhat different in that there is no relative shifting of time as in English.

**==> picture [162 x 226] intentionally omitted <==**

**----- Start of picture text -----**<br>
If-whether Subordinate Clauses<br>MAIN CLAUSE IF / WHETHER SUBORDINATE CLAUSE<br>PRESENT INDICATIVE PRESENT INDICATIVE<br>At utdide ven it te ha vyan.<br>I wonder if / whether he knows the truth.<br>PRESENT INDICATIVE PAST INDICATIVE<br>At voy te ven yit aka ey oka.<br>I don't know if / whether they won or lost.<br>PRESENT INDICATIVE FUTURE INDICATIVE<br>At voy te ven et ujako.<br>I don't know if / whether you will succeed.<br>PRESENT INDICATIVE PRESENT HYPOTHETICAL<br>At utdide ven et yantexu.<br>I wonder if / whether you would agree.<br>PAST INDICATIVE PRESENT INDICATIVE<br>At voy ta ven wit se taduwa.<br>I didn't know if / whether he was [Mirad: is] married.<br>PAST INDICATIVE PAST INDICATIVE<br>At dida ven iyt teata hia dezun.<br>I asked if / whether she had seen [Mirad: saw] this play.<br>PAST INDICATIVE FUTURE INDICATIVE<br>At voy ta ven it upo<br>I didn't know if / whether he would [Mirad: will] come.<br>PAST INDICATIVE PRESENT HYPOTHETICAL<br>At dida ven it fu per bay at.<br>I asked if / whether he might like to go with me.<br>PAST INDICATIVE PAST HYPOTHETICAL<br>At dida ven it fayu per bay at.<br>I asked if / whether he might have liked to go with me.<br>**----- End of picture text -----**<br>

The negative conditional complementizer **oven** .... _unless_ is used in main-subordinate clause structures in the same way as the above.

## **Relative Clauses**

_**Relative clauses**_ are of two types:

_**Bound relative clauses**_ qualify an explicit element (usually a noun or phrase) appearing in the main clause, and refer back to that element by means of the relative complementizer **ho** (example: "The boy who laughed was expelled."), and:

_**Free relative clauses**_ , which do not have an explicit antecedent external to themselves. Instead, the relative clause itself takes the place of an argument in the matrix clause. For example, in the English sentence _I like what I see_ , the clause _what I see_ is a free relative clause, because it has no antecedent, but itself serves as the object of the verb like in the main clause. (An alternative analysis is that the free relative clause has zero as its antecedent.) In Mirad, relative deictic pronouns or adverbs having the prefix **ho** , as shown in the chart below, are used to introduce the free relative clause.

## **Bound Relative Clauses**

The invariable relative complementizer **ho** is used to introduce a bound relative clause and refer back to an element in the main clause. Here are some examples:

**Ha tob, ho tadsa ewa jabi jay, ayse awa tud.** .... _The man, who got married two years ago, has one child._

**Ha toyb ho ako ibo aga nazun.** .... _The woman who wins will receive a big prize._

**Hia pati ho at pixahisi magelwo himaj.** .... _These birds (that/which) I caught will be cooked this evening._ **Biu hyea jotul ho et fu.** .... _Take any dessert (that) you'd like._

**Ha apet ho at bua it ha afeb apeda bay if.** .... _The horse I gave the apple to neighed with pleasure._ (= _...that I gave him the apple..._ )

**Iyt trua at bu ha yexeb ho iyt yexaya oyb it ji gla jabi.** .... _She introduced me to the boss under whom she had worked for many years._ (Lit: _...that she had worked under him..._ )

In cases where the antecedent in the matrix clause needs to be very clear, **ho** can be replaced with a relative pronoun specifying the gender or number of the antecedent, for example:

**Ata tedi ay yita tuyd, hoyt at yuxa be ha aj,...** .... _My parents and their daughter, whom (f.s. referring to the daughter) I helped in the past, ..._ **Ata tedi ay yita tuyd, hoti at yuxa be ha aj,...** .... _My parents and their daughter, whom (pl.) referring to both the parents and their daughter) I helped in the past, ..._

**Ata tedi ay yita tuyd, ho at yuxa iyt be ha aj,...** (Here the relative complementizer **ho** is used but is followed up later with a resumptive feminine personal pronoun. For consistence in the

140 of 158

Mirad Grammar/print version - Wikibooks, open books for an open world

language, this latter method is best.)

Note that in cases where the relative clause ends in a preposition governing the man clause antecedent, a _**resumptive pronoun**_ is added agreeing in gender, number, and animacy with the main clause antecedent. This type of construction occurs in the last two example sentences above. So, the English relative clause _for whom I sang_ would be expressed in Mirad as _that I sang for her/him /it/them_ depending on the gender, number, and animacy of the antecedent in the main clause.

**Ha toybi ho at deuza av yiyt fida ata yafi.** .... _The ladies for whom I sang (= that I sang for them) praised my abilities._

Bound relative clauses beginning with _whose_ are expressed in Mirad as **hota** ( _which person's_ ) or **hoyita** (which persons'), depending on the number of the explicit antecedent in the main clause.

**Ha ekuyt hota tyoyab yonpyexwa yofa eker hijeb.** .... _The female player whose foot was broken was unable to play this season._

**Ata yubati, hoyita tam se jay ga aga vyel yatas, agaxa yita puram gajod.** .... _Our neighbors, whose (= which persons') house is already bigger than ours, enlarged their garage again._

If no preposition governing the antecedent is involved, but the relative clause takes the place of an objective case element, supplying a pronoun referring back to the antecedent noun (resumptive pronoun) is optional:

**Ha dyesi ho at dyea hasi zamaj sa hyasi fia.** .... _The books (which) I read (them) last evening were all good._

## **Free Relative Clauses**

Free relative clauses are introduced by a relative deictic pronoun or adverb as shown in the charts below. Note that if the deictic pronoun is one other than a relative pronoun or adverb, then it is followed by the relative complementizer **ho** . For example, **Hos at te...** .... _What I know_ does not need the relative complementizer **ho** , because it is already embedded in the relative pronoun **hos** . The use of **ho** with other deictic words in a relative clause is optional.

**==> picture [412 x 274] intentionally omitted <==**

**----- Start of picture text -----**<br>

What I said is true.<br>hosi .... what/those which/the things that Hosi it xa futipxa at. .... What/the things he did angered me.<br>hyes (ho) .... whatever/anything that At xo hyes (ho) et do. .... I will do whatever/anything you say.<br>hyesi (ho) .... whatever/anything that/any things that Et voy teeta hyesi (ho) at deuza. .... You didn't hear any of the things I sang.<br>Thing(s) hyas (ho)hyasi (ho) ........ everything that/all thatall (things) that Hyas At akxa (hohyas (ho) at fe se poos.) at fa. ....... I achieved . The town where I come from is very small.<br>bu hom .... to where, whither Ha memi hom at popeyo se gle jiba. .... Do it the same way as I do it.<br>Degree hoglahyigla ( ~ ge) ho .... how, to what extent .... as, to the same degree as Et hyoj to At yofe poperhoglahogla ( iva at se.= ge) yib ho  .... You'll never know et yafe. .... I cannot travelhow happy I am.as far as you can.<br>hogla .... how much, how many Duven et te hogla nas it ayse? .... You will earn as much money as I do.<br>Reason hosavhyesav (ho) .... why, for what reason .... why ever, for whatever reason Duven et teYat voy testehosav hyesav it xa hus.(ho) et xu hus. .... Do you know .... We don't understandwhy he did that?why ever you'd do that.<br>**----- End of picture text -----**<br>

The **ho** complementizer in free relative clauses can be omitted in conversation if there is no loss of meaning. For example, **At fe per hyem et pe.** .... _I want to go wherever you go._ or **Xu geyen at**

**de.** .... _Do as (= the same way (that)) I say._

If the relative clause is restrictive (i.e. it cannot be omitted without violating the meaning of the sentence), then no commas are used, but if it is non-restrictive (i.e. it provides new information that can be omitted), then it is surrounded by commas, just as in English.

RESTRICTIVE: **Ha mar ho yata mer yuzpe dyunwe ha maar.** .... _The star that our planet goes around is called the sun._

NON-RESTRICTIVE: **Ha maar, ho yata mer yuzpe, se vay haway hea mar.** .... _The sun, which our planet goes around, is really only a (= some) star._

## **Indirect and Direct Discourse**

As in English, Mirad has both indirect discourse and direct discourse. Indirect discourse is when you know or say _that something happened_ , whereas direct discourse is when you directly quote what someone has said.

## **Indirect Discourse**

Sentences that have a main clause of communication or knowledge, followed by a subordinate clause with an indirect indication of what was said or known, use the positive complementizer **van** ( _that, the fact that_ ) to introduce the subordinate clause. The tense in the subordinate clause is a true tense, not a relative tense. Unlike in English, where the _that_ can often be omitted, the Mirad **van** complementizer can never be omitted.

**At ta van et upo.** .... _I knew that you would (= will) come._

**Ata ted da van it yexe hya ita tej gel fufut.** .... _My father said that he had worked (= he worked) all his life as a plumber._

**Se vyaa van at gra tele.** .... _It is true that I eat too much._

**At jada van et puo jwa.** .... _I predicted that you would (= you will) arrive early._

The conditional complementizer **ven** .... _if, whether_ and the negative complementizer **von** .... _lest, don't, that...not_ are discussed in later sections.

## **Direct Discourse**

Direct discourse works as in English, except that a colon (:) is used instead of a comma. Double quotes are used to surround the directly quoted part of the sentence.

**Iyt da: "At voy fe per."** .... _She said, "I don't want to go."_

**At dida it: "Duhot so eta aadezut?".** .... _I asked him, "Who will be your lead actor?"_

## **The Object**

The object in a sentence can be noun or noun phrase, a pronoun, an infinitive, a gerund, a prepositional phrase, or a clause. Sometimes, an object consists of both a direct object and an indirect object.

Rules:

141 of 158

Mirad Grammar/print version - Wikibooks, open books for an open world

**==> picture [466 x 263] intentionally omitted <==**

**----- Start of picture text -----**<br>
Transitive verbs can take a direct object:<br>Ha yepet teupixa at. .... The dog bit me.<br>Yovobu hoti fyuxe et. .... Forgive those who hurt you.<br>Biu hia yibdren. .... Take this telegram.<br>Some transitive verbs can take both a direct and indirect object. Many common transitive verbs imply a directional proposition, and so that preposition need not be expressed in the<br>indirect object, but in such cases the indirect object comes before the direct object:<br>Buu at hua nyem. .... Give (to) me that box.<br>Du it doler. .... Tell (to) him to be quiet.<br>Xu at ha avun bi pier. .... Do (to) me the favor of leaving.<br>Stative intransitive verbs like  ser  ( to be ) can be followed by a complement consisting of a noun, pronoun, adjective, infinitive, gerund, or clause.<br>His se fis. .... This is a good thing.<br>His se gla fia. .... This is very good.<br>Ha akut sa et. .... The winner was you.<br>Se fia aker. .... It is good to win.<br>Se uva van iyt pia. .... It is sad that she left.<br>Wit tease fia yexut. .... He looks like a good worker.<br>Dynamic intransitive verbs do not take an object:<br>At yexa hum je ewa jabi. .... I worked there for two years.<br>Yat teje yukomay. .... We live comfortably.<br>Hia voli agse ug. .... These plants grow slowly.<br>Verbs of communication can take an entire clause as a direct object in addition to an indirect object, the recipient of the communication:<br>At ta van et upo. .... I knew (that) you would come.<br>Duven et te hoa tam se itas? .... Do you know which house is his?<br>At da it hom et tambee. .... I told him where you live.<br>Tuu at hoj et puo. .... Inform me when you arrive.<br>It voy da ven et upo. .... He did not say whether he would be coming.<br>At jwatua von it jwosu. .... I warned him not to be late (= lest he be late).<br>Verbs of motion and communication, which have an inherent directional component implied, do not need a preposition before their object. In cases where there is both an indirect and<br>direct object, the indirect object comes before the direct object, otherwise a preposition is necessary:<br>At peye ha nam. .... I'm going to the store. ( = I'm going the store.)<br>Pu tam! .... Go home!<br>Et yefu der iyt hus. .... You should tell her that.<br>Ha tob zoyda at: "Va." .... The man replied to me, "Yes." ( = replied me)<br>At byise Ferom. .... I come from France. ( = I originate France)<br>Nusbiu at dyes. (or) Nusbiu dyes av at. .... Buy me a book (or) Buy a book for me.<br>**----- End of picture text -----**<br>

## **Article One of the Declaration of Human Rights**

_**Article One of the Declaration of Human Rights**_ is often used to show how various invented international auxiliary languages compare with one another in written form. Here is the Mirad version of Article One, followed by the English version:

- **Declaration of Human Rights Article One**

- **ENGLISH MIRAD**

- _All human beings are born free and equal in dignity and rights. They are endowed with reason and conscience and should act towards one_ **Hya tobi taje yiva ay gea be utfiz ay doyivi. Yit bulwe bay vyatex ay tyaf ay yeyfe** _another in a spirit of brotherhood._ **hyuitaxler tidyenay.**

- Anaysis: 1 **hya** _all_ < **hya-** [distributive deictic determiner]   + 2 **tobi** _human beings_ < **tob** .... _human being_ [singular noun]   + **-i** [plural suffix] 3 **taje** _are born_ < **taj-** .... _be born_ [stem])  + **-e** [present simple tense marker] 4 **yiva** _free_ < **yiv-** [stem]   + **-a** [adjectival suffix] 5 **ay** _and_ [positive conjunction] 6 **gea** _equal_ < **ge-** [stem]   + **-a** [adjectival suffix] 7 **be** _at, in_ [preposition] 8 **utfiz** _dignity_ < **ut** .... _self_ [pronoun]  + **fiz** .... _merit_ [noun] 9 **doyivi** _rights_ < **do(t)-** .... _society_ + **yiv** .... _freedom, right_ [noun]  + **-i** [plural suffix] 10 **yit** _they/them_ < **yit** [3d person plural animate pronoun] 11 **bulwe** _are endowed_ < **bul-** .... _endow_ [verb stem]   + **-w** [passive]   + **-e** [present] 12 **bay** _with_ [preposition] 13 **vyatex** _reason_ < **vya-** .... _true, right_ + **tex** .... _thought_ 14 **tyaf** _conscience_ < **t-** .... _know_ + **yaf** .... _ability, faculty_ 15 **yeyfe** _should_ < **yeyf-** .... _(have a) duty_ [verb stem]   + **-e** [indicative simple present tense] 16 **hyuitaxler** _treat one another_ < **hyuit** (comb. of **hyut** .... _other person_ + **hyit** .... _same person_ )   + **axl-** .... _act_ [verb stem]   + **-er** [verbal infinitive marker] 17 **tidyenay** _in a brotherly way_ < **tid** .... _sibling_ [noun]   + **-yen** .... _manner_ + **-ay** .... _-ly_ [adverbial suffix]

## **Lord's Prayer**

Word-for-word analysis:

|**The Lord's Prayer**||
|---|---|
|**ENGLISH**<br>**MIRAD**||
|_Our Father, who art in Heaven,_<br>**Hey yata Twed, ho se be Totmir,**||
|_Hallowed by thy name._<br>**van eta dyun fyadwu.**||
|_Thy kingdom come._<br>**Van eta edob upu.**||
|_Thy will be done on Earth as it is in Heaven._<br>**Van eta fon xwu be Imer hoyen xwe be Totmir.**||
|_Give us this day our daily bread,_<br>**Buu yat hijub yata hyajuba ovol,**||
|_and forgive us our trespasses_<br>**ay yovobu yat bi yata fuxeyni**||
|_as we forgive those who trespass against us._<br>**hoyen yat yovobe hoti fuxe yat.**||
|_And lead us not into temptation,_<br>**Ay von izbu yat ub fuyekuen,**||
|_But deliver us from evil._<br>**oy yivxu yat bi fyox.**||
|_Amen._<br>**Su huuyen.**||
|1<br>**Hey**<br>_O!_[vocative particle]||
|2<br>**yata**<br>_our_<_at_[1st sing animate pronoun]_I/me_+_-i_[plural] +**-a**[adjective suffix]||
|3<br>**Twed**<br>_Father_<**ted**...._parent_+ infix**-w-**[masculine]||
|4<br>**ho**<br>_who_[invariable relative complementizer meaning_who(m), that, which_]||
|5<br>**se**<br>_am,is,are_<**s-**[present stem of verb**ser**...._to be_] +**-e**[present tense suffix]||
|6<br>**be**<br>_in_[preposition of location_at_]||
|7<br>**Totmir**<br>_Heaven_<**tot**...._god_+**mir**...._world_||
|8<br>**van**<br>_let/may/that_[positive complementizer introducing a fact or wish; see 32]||
|9<br>**eta**<br>_your, thy_<**et**[2d sing animate pronoun]_you_+**-a**[adjective suffix]||
|10**dyun**<br>_name_[noun < verb stem**dyu-**...._to call_]||
|11 **fyadwu**<br>_be blessed_< fya-_holy_+**d-**[stem of verb_say / call_] +**-w-**[passive] +**-u**[hypothetical/imperative/subjunctive mood]||

142 of 158

Mirad Grammar/print version - Wikibooks, open books for an open world

12 **edob** _kingdom_ < **e-** [2nd level of scalar noun base **dob** .... _state_ ] 13 **upu** _come_ < **u(b)34** - _toward_ + **p** [stem of verb _to go_ ] + **-u** [hypothetical/imperative/subjunctive mood] 14 **fwas** _will_ < **f-** [stem of verb _to want_ ] + **-w-** [passive voice] + **-a** [adjective] + **-s** [inanimate nominalizer _thing_ ] = **wanted thing** 15 **xwu** _be done_ < **x-** [stem of verb _to do_ ] + **-w-** [passive voice] + **-u** [hyp./imper./subj.] 16 **Imer** _earth_ < **-i-** [3d level of scalar noun **mer** .... _planet_ ] = _third planet from the sun_ 17 **hoyen** _as_ < **ho** [relative determiner prefix] + **-yen** [suffix = _manner_ ] **hoyen** = _(which manner that)_ 18 **xwe** _(it) is done_ < **x-** [stem of verb _to do_ ] + **-w-** [passive voice] + **-e** [present simple tense] 19 **Buu** _Give_ < **bu-** [stem of verb _to give_ ] + **-u** [hyp./imper./subj.] 20 **yat** _(to) us_ < **at** [1st sing pron _I/me_ ] + **-i** [plural] 21 **hijub** _today, this day_ < **hi-** [proximate determiner _this_ ] + **jub** .... _day_ 22 **yata** _our_ < **at** [1st sing pron _I/me_ ] + **-i** [plural] + **-a** [adjective suffix] 23 **hyajuba** _daily_ < **hya-** [distributive determiner _every_ ] + **jub** .... _day_ + **-a** [adjective suffix] 24 **ovol** _bread_ [ < **ovob** .... _cereal_ with **b** (plant) -> **l** (food)] 25 **ay** _and_ [positive conjunction] ( **ey** [intermediate] = _or_ , **oy** [negative] = _but_ ) 26 **yovobu** _forgive_ < **yov** .... _guilt, shame_ + **ob** [preposition _off_ and stem of verb _to remove_ ] + **-u** [hyp./imper./subj.] 27 **bi** _from_ [preposition meaning _of, from_ ; opp: **bu** .... _to_ ] 28 **fuxeyni** _bad deeds_ [noun] < **fu-** .... _bad_ + **-xeyn-** .... **deed** + **-i** [plural suffix' 29 **yovobe** _forgive_ < **yov** .... _guilt, shame_ + **ob** [proposition _off_ and stem of verb _to remove_ ] + **-e** [present] 30 **hoti** _those who_ < **ho-** [relative deictic determiner] + **-t** .... _person_ + **-i** [plural suffix] 31 **fuxe** _offend_ < **fu** .... _bad_ + **-x-** .... _do_ + **-e** [present] 32 **von** _lest, so not, don't_ [negative complementizer; **van** [positive] _that/so that/let_ ; **ven** [intermediate] _if, whether_ ] 33 **izbu** _lead, guide_ < **iz** .... _direct, straight_ + **b-** [stem of verb _put_ ] + **-u** [hyp./imper./subj.] 34 **ub** _toward_ [preposition; opp. **ib** .... _away_ ] 35 **fuyekuen** _temptation_ < **fu-** .... _bad_ + **yek-** [stem of verb _try_ ] + **-u-** [causative formant] + **-en** [present gerund _-ing_ ] = _causing (someone) to try (something)_ 36 **oy** _but_ [negative conjunction; see 25] 37 **yivxu** _deliver, free, liberate_ < **yiv-** .... _free_ + **-x-** .... _do, make_ + **-u** [hyp./imper./subj.] 38 **fyox** _evil_ < **fyo-** .... _profane, evil_ + **x** .... _doing_ 39 **su** _be_ < **s-** [stem of verb _to be_ ] + **-u** [hyp./imper./subj.] 40 **huuyen** _thus, such a way_ < **huu-** [deictic determiner _such_ ] + **-yen** .... _manner, way_

## **Tower of Babel**

**==> picture [498 x 515] intentionally omitted <==**

**----- Start of picture text -----**<br>
ENGLISH MIRAD<br>The Tower of Babel Ha Yabtom bi Babel<br>Then, all earthly humans had a single language and a common vocabulary. Huj, hya imertobi bexa ana dalzeyn ay yansauna dunyan.<br>While people were migrating from the east, they discovered a plain in the region of Shenear and they settled there. Je van tobi emuipeya byi ha zimerem, yit yokkaxa zyimem be ha meam "Xenear" ay yit tamkyoxahum.<br>The people said to one another, "Come on, let's mold some bricks and fire them." Thus, they had bricks for building Ha tobi hyuitda: "Upu, van yat sanxu hegla mefi ay magxu isi." Huyen, yit bexa mefi av sexmegi ay<br>stones and tar for mortar. megyel av sexyanul.<br>Then, the people said, "Come on, let's build our own city with a tower reaching the sky. In that way, we will be famous Johus, ha tobi da: "Upu, van yat sexu yauta dom bay yabtom pyusea ha mam. Huyen, yat so<br>and that will prevent us from being scattered all over the earth." yibtrawa ay hus jaebo yata yonzyaben bu hyami bi ha imer."<br>The Eternal one came down from the sky to see the city with the tower the people of earth had constructed. Ha Hyajeseat yopa bi ha mam av teater ho dom bay ho yabtom ha imerati sexaya.<br>Then, the Eternal One said, "Behold, they make up one people, all of whom have a common language. This is only their Johus, ha Hyajeseat da, "Teaxu: Yit sanse ana tyob, ho hyati bexe yansauna dalyen. His se anay<br>first accomplishment. After this, anything they plan will be realizable." yita aa xal. Johis, hyes yit ojtexo so vyamxyafwa.<br>Come, let us go down there to confuse their language so they won't understand one another anymore." Upu, van yat yopu hum av yanmulxer yita dalzeyn von yit hyuittestu gaj."<br>Then the Eternal one scattered the men far from there to all parts of the earth, and they halted construction of the city Johus ha Hyajeseat yonzyaba ha tobi yib bi hum ub hyami bi ha imer, ay yit poxa ha sexen bi ha<br>and tower. dom ay yabtom.<br>That is why this place was named Babel, i.e. "Confusion". It is where the Eternal One mixed up the languages of all Hus se hosav him dyunxwa Babel, be hyua duni: "Yanmulx". Se hom ha Hyajeseat vyonapxa ha<br>humans and scattered them all over the earth. dalzeyni bi hya imerati ay yonzyaba yit bu hyami bi ha imer.<br>Word-for-word analysis:<br>1.<br>ha .... the  [definite determiner]<br>yabtom .... tower  <  yab- .... high  +  tom .... building<br>bi .... of, from  [preposition; opp:  bu .... to ]<br>Babel  [proper name]<br>huj .... then  <  hu-  [distal determiner  that ] +  j  [stub for  job .... time ]<br>hya .... all  [distributive determiner]<br>imertobi .... people of earth  <  imer .... earth  [ = planet 3] +  tob .... human  +  -i  [plural marker]<br>bexa .... had  <  bex-  [verb stem of  to have/hold ] +  -a  [past tense]<br>ana .... a single  <  a(n)- .... one  +  -a  [adjective marker]<br>dalzeyn .... language  <  dal .... speech  +  zeyn  medium<br>ay .... and  [positive conjunction; opp:  oy .... but ]<br>yansauna .... common  <  yan- .... together  +  saun .... type  +  -a  [adjective marker]<br>dunyan .... vocabulary  <  dun' .... word  +  -yan .... collection<br>1.<br>je van .... while  <  je .... during  +  van  [positive complementizer]  that<br>tobi .... men, people  <  tob  [noun]  person/man/human  +  -i  [plural marker]<br>emuipeya .... were migrating  <  em .... place  +  ui- .... hither-thither  +  p- ... go  +  -ey-  [progressive aspect] +  -a  [past tense]<br>byi .... since, starting with  [preposition; opp:  byu .... up to ]<br>zimerem .... east  <  zi-  =  right/east  +  mer .... planet  +  -em .... location<br>yit .... they, them  <  yit  [3d plur animate pronoun]<br>yokkaxa .... discovered  <  yok .... surprise  +  kax-  [stem of verb  find ] +  -a  [past simple tense marker]<br>zyimem .... a plain  <  zyi- .... flat  +  mem .... land<br>tamkyoxa .... settled  <  tam  =  home  +  kyox- .... fix  +  -a  [past tense marker]<br>hum .... there  <  hu-  [distal determiner  that ] +  -m'  [suffix of  place ]<br>1.<br>hyuitda .... said to one another  <  hyuit  <  hyui- .... one-another  +  -t  [ person  suffix] +  d-  [stem of verb  say,tell ] +  -a  [past tense maker]<br>van .... that  < [positive complementizer  that, let, so that ]<br>yat .... we, us  [1st plur anim pron]<br>sanxu .... form, mold  <  san .... form  +  -x- .... do/make/-ify  +  -u  [hypothetical/imperative/subjunctive]<br>hegla .... some  <  he-  [indefinite determiner prefix  some ] +  -gla  [determiner suffix  quantity/amount/degree ]<br>mefi .... bricks  <  mef  [noun]  brick  +  -i  [plural marker]<br>magxu .... fire, burn  <  mag-  =  fire  +  -x- .... do/make/-ify  +  -u  [hypothetical/imperative/subjunctive]<br>isi .... they, them  <  isi  [inanimate 3p plur pronoun]<br>huyen .... thus, so  <  hu-  [distal determiner prefix  that ] +  -yen  [determiner suffix  manner ]<br>av .... for  [preposition; opp:  ov .... against ]<br>sexmegi .... building stones  <  sex-  [stem of verb  to build ] +  meg .... stone  +  -i  [plural marker]<br>megyel .... tar, pitch, asphalt  <  meg .... stone  +  -yel  [suffix  viscous liquid ]<br>sexyanul .... mortar  <  sex-  [stem of verb  to build ] +  yan  =  together  +  -ul .... substance<br>**----- End of picture text -----**<br>
